Municipal Government Representatives Returning to Shanghai from Iron Department Meeting 140

The Songhu Road Returned to Municipal Management – A Satisfactory Result

Previously, for the sake of developing the downtown area, the Shanghai Municipal Government consulted with the Ministry of Railways to transfer the management rights of the Songhu Road to the Municipal Government for handling. The Ministry of Railways convened a meeting in Nanjing on July 30th to discuss this. The Municipal Government also sent Public Utilities Bureau Director Huang Boqiao and Public Works Bureau Director Shen Yi to Beijing to participate. Both Shen and Huang have already returned to Shanghai and reported the details of their trip to Beijing to Mayor Wu. A reporter from the Central News Agency went to the Public Works Bureau yesterday to interview Director Shen, who stated that he (Shen) and Director Huang were ordered to go to Beijing to participate in the Ministry of Railways meeting. Attendees included the two representatives from the Municipal Government, Minister Gu, Vice Minister Zeng, and various department and section chiefs from the Ministry of Railways. The mission of the Municipal Government representatives was to report the actual situation in Shanghai and explain to the Ministry of Railways the reasons for requesting the transfer of management of the Songhu Road. This was because the Songhu Road is actually one of the most important tasks for the future development of the downtown area. Considering the Songhu Road as it is today, it not only fails to aid the development of the downtown area but also presents various obstacles to development. Therefore, the Municipal Government intends to request the transfer of management rights in order to renovate and reorganize the Songhu Road. Currently, the Ministry of Railways is quite considerate of the issue of municipal development in Shanghai. Therefore, the Ministry has indicated that it will consider the various points reported by the Municipal Government representatives. For example, regarding the North Station relocation issue, the Ministry of Railways has notified the Municipal Government that the area south of Shida Road will be used as the main passenger station, and the area west of Zhenbei Road will be the site for the joint operation station of the Jinghu and Huhang railways. This decision does not entail any benefit for the Ministry of Railways but has a significant impact on the municipal development of Shanghai. Therefore, the results of this trip to Beijing are considered satisfactory.

Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau Ordered to Act as Treasury for Ministry of Communications 141

The Shanghai Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau received an order yesterday from the Ministry of Communications to act as the ministry's treasury. All subordinate agencies, whether operational or non-operational, are required to deposit all funds exceeding fifty yuan into the remittance bureau in their respective locations, as funds to be transferred to the ministry. Expenditures are also to be drawn monthly from the respective remittance bureaus according to the original budget. In case of special needs, approval must be obtained from the ministry before funds can be withdrawn. The ministry has also issued a notice to all subordinate agencies. Company Law Amendment Extension Again 143

Ministry of Industry Ordered National Federation of Commerce to Notify

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce received an instruction yesterday from the Ministry of Industry stating that the deadline for amending company charters has expired again. Starting from July 1st of this year, the deadline is extended for another six months. The original order stated: "Regarding compliance matters, it has been found that some provisions of the company charters conflict with the Company Law. According to the law, these provisions should be amended and submitted for approval within six months after the implementation of the Company Law. By the end of December of the twentieth year, when the deadline expired, reasons for extending the deadline were duly prepared and submitted to the Executive Yuan, which approved an extension of six months. The ministry has notified all provincial and municipal governments to comply accordingly. Now, this deadline has expired again on June 30th of this year. Many companies in various locations have made amendments in accordance with the law, but many others have been unable to make amendments on time due to various difficulties. Moreover, the charters of these companies were originally approved as valid documents, and there was no legal deadline for amendment under the old law. It is only because the new law has been implemented that conflicts cannot be allowed to persist indefinitely. The short deadline was intended to ensure that everyone complies with the new law as soon as possible. Now that amendments cannot be completed within the deadline, in order to sympathize with the difficulties of businesses and ensure that the charters of all companies comply, the Executive Yuan has issued Instruction No. 1838, approving an extension of another six months starting from July 1st of this year." In addition to separate notifications, this order is hereby issued for notification and compliance. All companies that have not yet amended their charters in accordance with the law must comply, make amendments, and report them promptly without further delay. This order.

Soliciting Designs for Chinese Pavilion at American Exposition 149

The United States will hold a Centennial Progress Exposition in Chicago on June 1st next year. Our country has decided to participate and established a preparatory committee on June 15th. The committee has leased a site at the Chicago venue, totaling one acre, or 43,560 square feet. It is now actively preparing to build the Chinese Pavilion, with two-fifths of the area dedicated to the pavilion. The architectural style has been set as purely Chinese to represent Chinese culture and art. The construction cost is limited to US$30,000. The remaining two-fifths of the land will be used to arrange surrounding scenery and attach several outbuildings, with a cost not exceeding US$10,000. The exposition will only last for 150 days, so the construction only needs to take six months. The materials used do not need to be overly sturdy or expensive. Furthermore, the committee is widely soliciting designs in order to obtain the best design. All architects registered with the Ministry of Industry can apply. The deadline is August 20th for this city and August 30th for other cities. The selected designs will be awarded certificates by the Ministry of Industry and a reward of 500 national currency. Detailed topographic maps of the Chinese Pavilion can be obtained from the committee inside the International Trade Bureau on Hankou Road.

Local News Two

Indian Police Prevent Moving, Actually Stabbing Tenant to Death 150

Four Others Stabbing Wounded at the Same Time – Great Disturbance in Lizhong Lane – All Five Murderers Are Indians – Extrajudicial Murder Should Be Severely Punished

The Lizhong Lane at the end of Yuezhou Road experienced a case of Indian police stabbing a Chinese person to death yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM. The detailed circumstances are recorded below.

The Topography of Lizhong Lane Lizhong Lane is located at the intersection of the Chinese concession of Yuezhou Road and Linping Road. There are more than one hundred houses in it. The area near Yuezhou Road is governed by the Huishan Police, accounting for about one-third of the total. The remaining two-thirds are managed by the Third Sub-bureau of the Fifth District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau. Usually, Chinese and concession police are dispatched to patrol from time to time. The big landlord is Chen Changkun, who works as a carpenter. He runs the Chen Wanxing Wood Shop at the intersection of Hailer Road and Oujia Road in this city. Last autumn, the landlord and tenants once litigated over the issue of rent increases. Chen lost the case, so he entrusted the entire management of the lane to the China Business Company at 70 Sichuan Road for management.

The Tyranny of the Four Indian Police After being authorized, the China Business Company hired four Indian police to take turns guarding the houses in the lane. The hired Indian police were named Yousha, Shamingen, Aili Haitai, and Manhuasigen. However, these four Indian police often threatened the residents in the lane, or even used torture. By the spring of this year, when the January 28th Incident occurred, the residents in the lane all fled with their families. The four Indian police took the opportunity to extort movers in every possible way. If they were not satisfied, they would wield knives. At that time, the tenant association of the lane reported to the Huishan Police Station, and the matter subsided slightly. In April, when the tenants gradually moved back, the Indian police relapsed. Therefore, conflicts arose. Afterwards, the Indian police stated that those who had moved in would never be allowed to move out again, but the tenants did not care.

Indian Police Forcibly Prevent Moving The rumors have been rampant in recent days, and the ignorant people have become panicked again. A tenant named Hong Kaifa, who is a carpenter, in Room 3, No. 28 of the lane, believed the rumors and invited his colleague Zhou Ayu to help him move yesterday (the 2nd) afternoon. Hong Kaifa was afraid that the Indian police would interfere, so he gave them one dollar in incense money in advance. Unexpectedly, the Indian police stated that it had to be four dollars, otherwise they would not let him go. Hong pleaded in every possible way, but to no avail. So Zhou Ayu suggested changing the route and going out of the lane through the Chinese boundary. While they were moving the furniture, an Indian police named Aladate, who was a gatekeeper in the Guangdong Brothers Rubber Company, had already tracked them down and came forward to stop them, and a dispute arose with Zhou and Hong. At the same time, the neighbors in the lane, seeing that the Indian police were unreasonable, all stood up for Zhou.

Zhou Ayu Stabbed to Death The Indian police were speechless and turned their anger into shame. Three of the Indian police pulled out sharp knives and stabbed at the crowd, and chased after Zhou Ayu. Seeing that the situation was not good, Zhou abandoned his belongings and ran wildly towards Linping Road. When he escaped to Renxin Lane, he was caught by the Indian police, who stabbed him in the left waist with a knife. Zhou fell to the ground and died. At this time, many residents were chasing after the Indian police. When Zhou was killed, the Indian police intended to turn back and escape into the concession. Seeing someone coming, they stabbed Yia San, Huang Ruifu, Cai Dianhua, and Xu Xiaocai, who were in front, with knives.

Five Murderers Arrested At that time, the Fifth District Third Sub-bureau had received a report from Dong Wu, the second landlord of Hong Kaifa. Patrol Officer Wang Yan led police chief Chen Yaxi and many police officers to the scene. Seeing that the matter involved a criminal case, they immediately arrested the murderers Yousha, Shamingen, and Aladate and detained them in the sub-bureau. Aili Haita and Manhuasigen intended to take the opportunity to escape. When they reached the entrance of Yuezhou Road, they were arrested by Huishan Police Nos. 2121 and 2010 and are now detained in the Huishan Police Station. The injured Yia San, Huang Ruifu, Cai Dianhua, and Xu Xiaocai were sent to Tongren Hospital for treatment by police cars. The murder weapon, three knives, are stored in the Fifth District Third Sub-bureau and the police station.

Emergency Meeting of Tenants The injured Yia San is from Jiangbei, 28 years old, and is a carriage driver, injured in the head. Huang Ruifu is from Ningbo, 40 years old, injured in the forehead. Cai Dianhua is from Jiangbei, 22 years old, injured in the back, and is the owner of Bao Shunhua Meat Shop. Xu Xiaocai is from Haimen, 24 years old, injured in the chest, and is a cattle slaughterer. The deceased Zhou Ayu was 26 years old, from Shaoxing, and worked as a carpenter. The corpse and the furniture boxes and baskets moved out by Zhou are displayed in the lane. The local court will send someone to inspect them at 10:00 AM this morning. At the same time, the tenant association of the lane convened an emergency meeting last night to jointly decide on a method and separately submitted it to the Taxpaying Chinese Association, the Lawyers Association, the Tenant General Association, the Six Townships Association, and the Ningbo Fellow-Provincial Association, requesting assistance.

The Commercial Press's Spirit of Service 151

The prosperous reopening of the Commercial Press's distribution office has been reported in yesterday's newspaper. It is now heard that in order to improve service efficiency, the office is having its staff provide sincere service and strive for promptness and thoroughness. It is also asking customers for supervision and guidance as a guideline for improvement. All employees wear numbered badges. A customer suggestion box has also been set up. Customers can express their suggestions in person to the director's office on the second floor or put them in the box in writing. In addition, a counter staff service competition method has been established. The office's publication counter, Western book counter, and stationery counter are each a battle position. Each counter is given 100 service points at the beginning of each month. If customers have any criticisms of the counter staff during the month, the evaluators will review and deduct points. According to the North China Daily News, American White Plaidburn, aged 74, loves to travel. He is known as the Marco Polo of the Americas. Saltpeter-Sulfur Boat Capsizes in Huangpu River 158

The Saltpeter-Sulfur Bureau of a certain organ of the National Government dispatched Yu Shunyuan to carry a list to the Yitaixing South Depot in Pudong at about 10:00 AM yesterday to pick up 50 barrels of saltpeter and sulfur. They ordered the pier boat of Song Longsheng to load them together, and hired the Xin Shunchang small wheel boat run by Sun Yusheng to tow the cargo ship to the Fair Road pier for unloading. Unexpectedly, when they arrived outside the Hongkou Port, the stern rudder of the cargo ship suddenly broke due to the impact of the tide, resulting in the loss of autonomy. It suddenly capsized, and the 50 barrels of saltpeter and sulfur it carried completely sank to the bottom of the river. Several boatmen also capsized under the boat. Fortunately, they were rescued from danger by the small wheel boat. Yu Shunyuan then took the old hands of both the small wheel boat and the cargo ship to the Customs Water Patrol Police Station to report the case and the reasons. The three parties returned to the Saltpeter-Sulfur Bureau to clarify which party should bear the responsibility for the losses incurred.

Lawsuit Involving a Man and a Dog Temporarily Suspended Due to Allegations of Bias by the Judge Chen Xinzhai, who pulls the bell at the Tianyun Building amusement park of Wing On Company, his wife Chen Lu, and Liu Xin'san, who teaches the games, were recently arrested by the Xinzha Police Station and sent to the First Special District Court. Wang Yaotang of the legal group filed a lawsuit against them for obscenity, enticing a black dog to have sexual intercourse with a young woman, and performing in various hotels for profit. Judge Wu Tingqi has questioned them twice, as reported in this newspaper. However, this case has undergone slight changes since the last adjournment. The defendants believe that Judge Wu is biased in the trial, so they entrusted their agent, Lawyer Gan Lin, to submit a petition to the Special Court, requesting Judge Wu to recuse himself. The petition stated that there was a risk of bias in the trial. The reason for requesting the judge's recusal was that the plaintiff made a living pulling the bell at the amusement park of Wing On Company, earning a monthly salary of 70 yuan. He has four adopted daughters, the eldest of whom is 11 years old. She learns the craft with him and can earn more than 20 yuan a month by going to the church at night, so his monthly income is not bad. However, he was recently arrested by the Xinzha Police Station, who said that he enticed a dog to have sexual intercourse with his adopted daughter and performed in hotels, so he was prosecuted according to law. Regardless of whether the matter is fabricated or there are other circumstances, the trial judge should investigate in detail to obtain the truth in order to be convincing. However, Judge Wu has preconceived notions and is biased against the defendant, which cannot be said to be doing his best in the trial. The legal articles cited by the police station refer to the suspicion of the plaintiff's dog having sexual intercourse with a person, which constitutes a crime. The plaintiff believes that he has never done such a thing, so he cannot be convicted of a crime. There are also many doubts in the legal text. Even if it is assumed that such a thing did happen, and there is a special article in the law, it should also be investigated whether there was sexual intercourse, which is the only key to establishing the crime. However, Judge Wu did not investigate this point. When the plaintiff's representative lawyer was permitted by Judge Wu to ask the plaintiff's daughter about this point, Judge Wu suddenly prohibited it. What was his intention? The plaintiff's daughter testified that when she was four years old, the plaintiff asked someone to train her to have sexual intercourse with a dog. However, the plaintiff's puppy was given to him by someone last year, which all the neighbors know. When the plaintiff's lawyer requested to call witnesses on this point, Judge Wu turned a deaf ear. How can it be said that he does not have preconceived notions and intentions of bias? Moreover, the injury report of the four daughters is too simple, only stating that the skin is broken. The plaintiff's lawyer requested a re-examination, but Judge Wu did not express permission. This point is consistent with the provisions of Article 27, Paragraph 2 of the Civil Procedure Law. Based on the above, Judge Wu has a risk of bias, so in accordance with Articles 27 and 28 of the Civil Law, this petition is submitted, requesting approval. Yesterday morning, this case was due for continued hearing. The Jiliang Institute also brought the four daughters, Chen Shuanglin, Genling, Guilin, and Caiyun, to the court. Judge Shen Zengshan still presided over the Second Criminal Court. The police lawyer, Wang Yaotang, recounted the case. Judge Wu then asked the defendants, Chen Xinzhai and Chen Lu, whether they had entrusted a lawyer to submit a petition. Chen et al. answered yes. Judge Wu then ordered Chen Xinzhai and Chen Lu to submit a petition for recusal, and the proceedings in this case should be suspended immediately. After the order was issued, the defendant's agent, Lawyer Gan, stood up and stated that there were two main points to report to the court: (1) Since the last court hearing, the defendant's buttocks have been beaten and swollen. (2) After this case occurred, someone introduced a lawyer to defend the defendant. This kind of lawyer introduction is not an illegal act. However, Chinese and foreign detectives from the police station led the defendant to the introducer's place a few days ago and searched it. This kind of illegal act should be urgently dealt with and remedied, etc. Judge Wu ordered to proceed separately according to law.

Three Girls Forced into Prostitution Temporarily Stay at the Jiliang Institute The case involves Chen Lianfang, a beautiful girl from Suzhou, and Zhu Huizhen, also from the same town, both 15 years old, and Xiao Jindi, a girl from Jiangbei, 18 years old, who was sold to Chen Mu, who lives at No. 5 Danshui Road, when she was young. International Trade Bureau of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce Publishes Wuhan Industry and Commerce Survey Report The International Trade Bureau of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, considering that the changes in Wuhan's industry and commerce after the flood were very significant and of great importance, sent personnel to conduct an on-site survey in April of this year. The place of distribution is the International Trade Bureau on the fourth floor of the Customs Building on Hankou Road, etc.

[White Jade] Paintbrushes Sell Very Well The paintbrushes used by Western painters in various countries have always been made in Japan [Hakugyoku]. Since the September 18th Incident, the trend of Chinese people automatically boycotting inferior goods has been very strong. The Nanyang Da Zhongwen Stationery Store in Shanghai created a [White Jade] paintbrush some years ago. It is both flexible and strong, and very easy to use, which is far superior to the inferior goods [Hakugyoku]. Recently, it has been improved to be even better. The sales are so strong that they have broken the silent record before the September 18th Incident. Free Talk

Talk of the Olympics by Zhan Lu

The World Olympic Games is going on in full swing. The 10th session is being held in Los Angeles, USA. The Republic of China, which calls itself an Olympic member state, only has one person, Liu Changchun, participating in this session. In that full swing, it only counts as a spark of fire and a leaf of tea. Among the flags of more than 50 countries, at least the flag of the Blue Sky White Sun is flying together. The heinous Manchu puppet state also wanted to send athletes, asking a midget to be their bodyguard, to Los Angeles to show off. After all, they got the cold shoulder, making fools of themselves. On this point, we Chinese people can at least let out this frustration.

In 1920, the 7th Olympic Games was held in Belgium. The United States sent representatives to request that the next games be held in Los Angeles. However, the meeting had already decided that the 8th session would be held in Paris, France, and the 9th session in The Hague, Netherlands. It was not until this session that Los Angeles was allowed to host. The construction of all the Olympic villages was contracted out by people for millions of dollars three years ago, making them magnificent and indescribably grand and great. They hired specialist chefs from 40 countries. The admission tickets had 15 different colors. When the poor and weak Chinese people see such a grand spectacle, how can they not feel their eyes burning with heat and their mouths watering?

In the past, we did not have Chinese athletes participating in the games because we gave up our rights. No matter how the meetings rotated, it would never be our turn to host. Now, we have Liu Changchun, who has planted a seed in the world of sports. In the future, one will become ten, and ten will become a hundred. More and more athletes will be sent. One day, we will build a magnificent Olympic village near our capital, welcoming athletes from all over the world to compete against each other. This is not me bragging, but there is a possibility in reality. It only requires political stability! It only requires striving towards the goal of strengthening the national physique!

Old Tales of Chen Yingshi by Zheng Yimei

The memorial tower of Chen Yingshi has already been erected at the intersection of Fangbang Road in Shanghai. Now, it is heard that a memorial hall will be established on Beijing Road. Those who held a spirit of great fearlessness before their death should be admired by future generations forever. A guest who was old friends with Mr. Yingshi described how Mr. Yingshi went to the Hu family to pay his respects. The Hu family used the Jiasheng Shousheng Monastery as the mourning hall. The guest was related to the Hu family and also went to socialize. Mr. Yingshi was at the same table that day. Mr. Yingshi had innovative ideas, saying that it was not suitable to set up a quiet Buddhist place in a prosperous city. These monasteries and temples could be rebuilt into libraries and memorial halls for celebrities. Those at the table who heard this did not take it seriously. Unexpectedly, after several years, Mr. Yingshi became a revolutionary pioneer with great enthusiasm. He succeeded and died. After several more years, the old site of Shousheng Monastery was actually changed into Chen Yingshi Memorial Hall, which is beautiful and grand. Together with the memorial tower in Ximen, they are two major buildings to commemorate his achievements. This was probably beyond Mr. Yingshi's expectations during his lifetime. The guest also said that Mr. Yingshi was good at telling jokes. A person from the state of Chu died in his residence nearby. The person from Chu indulged in licentious activities and lost his life. His death was not to be pitied, but they still euphemistically said that it was due to acclimatization and illness. Mr. Yingshi then cleverly constructed a joke, saying that a Buddhist woman caught a louse on her body. If she released it, she would feel the pain in her skin. If she pinched it, she would violate the precept of not killing. Faced with this dilemma, she deliberated again and again and then placed the louse in the hair on her head, saying, "It is not possible to release it, and it is even more impossible to pinch it. It is better to let it die from acclimatization." Those who heard this sighed repeatedly.

Therefore, after Nanjing strictly banned prostitution, the power of prostitution in Anqing suddenly became rampant. Recently, the new director of the Provincial Public Security Bureau, Zhang Benshun, took office.

River water is rising high. Anqing is usually eight or nine feet or one zhang above sea level. The river water is usually eight or nine feet or one zhang away from the shore. However, the local newspapers have not recorded this, and the construction authorities have not paid attention to this, which makes people even more strange.

The Newly Built Park Anqing has always lacked places for leisure. Even the Linghu Lake and Yingjiang Temple, which are known as scenic spots, are very ordinary. Although the area inside is not large, the layout is quiet and pleasant. What is especially special is that there are flower sheds and green shade everywhere. It has been extremely hot recently. Every evening, visitors flock to it. It has actually learned the style of the Bansong Garden in Shanghai. All kinds of cold food, snacks, and tea are available. It has indeed brought a lot of face to Anqing.

Summer in Xuanwu Lake by Sui Cheng

Among the lakes and marshes of the capital, Xuanwu Lake is the largest. There is a park on the lake with towering green trees and bamboo groves everywhere. Pavilions and waterside pavilions are connected by winding paths. The scenery is quiet and elegant, making it an excellent place to escape the summer heat. Every time the sun sets, you can see fashionable women and young boys coming in droves. Some row boats on the lake, and some enjoy tea in the park, using it to dispel the summer heat. However, the lake water is like soup in the evening. When the breeze passes, the heat makes people feel faint. The tourists do not know this. They feel uncomfortable with the warm wind after rowing only a few miles and abandon their boats to go ashore. This is very common. Therefore, those who visit the lake should first visit the park. When the night is late and they want to return, they should then row a boat. At this time, the heat in the lake water has been completely evaporated. A small boat drifts in the middle of the stream. The light breeze points to the clothes, and the body feels cool. When they reach the other shore, the noise and heat have been completely washed away.

There are those who sell tea in the park. They set up seats at will under the paulownia trees and beside the bamboo groves. They do not light lamps, but the bright moon shines on people. It is very quiet. Therefore, on the nights of the third and fifth days of the month, the seats are always full of guests. However, after the full moon, the round moon gradually wanes, and the starlight is also faint. Although there are many tourists, there are few who enjoy tea.

Domestic Factories Worth Introducing (15) by He Gongxing

(25) Machine-Made Cigarette Box Factory

The small cigarette boxes containing ten cigarettes are the most frequently sold and are shipped the fastest. They can be divided into two parts: the box shell and the box core.

Box Shell Making Method: (1) Use a small cutting knife to trim the printed paper with the trademark. (2) Use a scoring machine to score and cut it into paper strips. (3) Apply glue with a glue machine (some also use manual labor). (4) Cut the box shell. A machine can cut one million box shells per day. A cutting knife can cut 70,000 to 80,000 pieces per person per day. One person is in charge of the machine, pushing the box shell, which has already been glued into a long strip, into the machine. One side is pushed in, and the other side falls from the machine.

Box Core Making Method: There are large-scale and small-scale methods. For large-scale methods: (1) First, arrange the knives. The workers who arrange the knives must be top-notch workers, and their wages are often 50 or 60 yuan a month. (2) Use a printing cutting machine. If the box core needs to be printed with words, the machine can print, cut, and score the box core at the same time. (3) Separate the box cores manually. (4) Sand the edges. (5) Send them to a thousand to a bunch. For small-scale methods, except that the second step needs to be divided into three steps: cutting, printing, and scoring the box core, the rest is roughly the same.

The so-called large-scale equipment mentioned above is the Shanggong Machine-Made Cigarette Box Factory at the end of Zhoujiazui Road in Shanghai, which uses this method to manufacture. Its machines are American-style and self-made. Each machine can produce 2 million box

Appeal from the Egg Industry Guild 160

Petition to Withdraw the Newly Established Freight Rate Order

The transportation of egg yolks and whites was previously categorized as fourth class. Although the Ministry of Railways' new freight rate system in the 19th year of the Republic of China (1930) reclassified them as second and third class, the Egg Industry Guild repeatedly petitioned and was granted a temporary suspension of implementation. Unexpectedly, this year there is another order to collect fees according to the new freight rates, scheduled to take effect on August 1st. Yesterday, the Egg Industry Guild telegraphed the Ministry of Railways, requesting the withdrawal of the order. The telegram read: "Respectfully addressed to Minister Gu of the Nanjing Ministry of Railways: Regarding the freight classification of eggs, since the new regulations were revised in the 19th year of the Republic of China, we have repeatedly received your Ministry's understanding of the difficulties faced by businesses, continuing to charge according to the old classification. During this time, the egg industry has been as precarious as morning dew, and the extension of a lifeline until today has been entirely due to your Ministry's support. In May of this year, our fellow members suddenly received reports that egg freight rates would be charged according to the new classifications. In our anxious state, we painstakingly explained the decline of the egg industry over the years and petitioned your Ministry to postpone implementation, hoping to temporarily maintain the precarious situation. We have not yet received a response. We have recently learned that your Ministry has instructed all railways to immediately collect freight for egg transportation according to the grades specified in the newly revised freight classification table, with a trial period of one year, effective from August 1st. We believe that your Ministry's handling of egg freight rates involved issuing orders to various railways to solicit opinions, followed by discussions by the Freight Rate Committee, which cannot be said to be not cautious. If merchants could bear the burden, they would not dare to repeatedly petition. However, the egg industry is currently in a position of crisis. An investigation of the annual freight volume and revenue of various railways will confirm the industry's declining business. Further blows will inevitably lead to inability to sustain operations, resulting in closures. Your Ministry's intention to increase railway revenue will have the opposite effect, contradicting your Ministry's original intention of promoting national product exports. Furthermore, dried and fresh egg yolks and whites have historically been in the same class and could be packaged together. Now that they are classified into second and third classes, co-packaging is impossible, and there are no such large quantities for separate packaging. This is also a difficult problem to solve. Therefore, we urgently telegraph you, Minister, to promptly withdraw the order and instruct all railways to continue charging egg yolks and whites according to the fourth class to maintain the endangered industry. We are filled with trepidation as we await your command. The Shanghai Egg Industry Guild, respectfully."

Passenger Hangs Himself to Death Beside Bed 161

Around midnight the night before last, a passenger arrived at the Tongshang Hotel at No. 42 Avenue Road. He was dressed in a white silk long gown and appeared to be a merchant. The hotel waiter, Lu Xianzun, led him to room number 89. He paid the room fee and registered on the logbook as Zhou Zuofu, 28 years old, merchant. Shortly after, Zhou rang the bell. He gave the waiter one silver dollar, instructing him to buy snacks, fruit, soda, and white roses. After purchasing them, the waiter delivered the items and the change to Zhou. Zhou drank alone, appearing cheerful. The waiter closed the door and went back to his room to rest. Around 5 a.m., when the early shift waiter came on duty, he noticed the light was still on in room 89. He peered through the crack in the door and saw that the passenger was not in bed, arousing his suspicion. He ran to report to the front desk, and they retrieved a spare key. Opening the door, they found Zhou had used his belt to hang himself from the ceiling above the bed. Upon touching him, they found he was already dead. They immediately telephoned the Xinzha police station, and officer number 1425 arrived and transported the body to Renji Hospital, then to the forensic examination office on Fellen Road for examination. It is reported that the deceased left behind a pair of glasses, a wallet, and some double-copper coins, which the officer took to the police station for safekeeping.

Accomplice in the Liu Nianchun Kidnapping Case Held for Sentencing 164

Liu Nianchun, manager of the Dingkang Gold Shop at No. 516 Tianjin Road, resided at No. 922 North Chengdu Road. At 6 PM on July 5th of the year before last, he was kidnapped with his wife while sitting in their car. The kidnappers demanded 40,000 yuan. The family eventually paid 20,000 yuan for his release. The police later apprehended a kidnapper named Yu Baocheng, who confessed and was sentenced to death and executed. Previously, the Jiaxing Road police apprehended Shao A'gen, a Ningbo native and driver at the Lili Automobile Company on Suzhou Road. He denied involvement during questioning at the First Special District Court. The victim, Liu Nianchun, was also unable to identify him. The court ordered further investigation and summoned witnesses, as previously reported. Yesterday morning, Judge Shen Bingrong opened the court for interrogation. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin presented the case, stating that the original driver, surnamed Lu, was currently in the capital and requested to be questioned. Lu Liangyuan from Yangzhou testified that he was working at the Liu residence at the time, substituting for the car driver Lu Lanfu, who was ill. There were four kidnappers in total. One kidnapper boarded the car, pointed a gun at him, and forbade him from making any noise. They drove to Avenue Road, where the kidnappers forced him and the owner's wife (Liu's wife) out of the car, forbidding them to watch, under threat of death. Therefore, he could not identify the defendant. The defendant maintained his denial of being an accomplice. The court ordered arguments to begin. The police lawyer stated that Yu Baocheng, who was previously executed, had named an A'gen as participating in the kidnapping. The defendant was working as a driver at the Xinglong Automobile Company at the time and had pointed a gun at the victim. After the incident, the defendant worked as a driver for Attorney Zhang for only two days before going to Dalian. Therefore, the defendant was highly suspected. The defendant also retained a lawyer for defense. After reviewing the testimonies, Judge Shen ordered the defendant to be returned to custody for sentencing at a later date.

Jiangyin Gang vs. Shandong Gang in Pig Trade Fight 165

One Person Seriously Injured and Killed – Over Twenty People Detained

Xuejiabang is a pig market wharf in Nanshi, with rows of pig traders and workers, each with their own faction. Long-standing grievances had accumulated. Sun Jiwu, a Shandong native employed by a pig trader, was attacked on the morning of the 31st of last month, around 7 a.m., while walking out of the Changchunlou teahouse in Xuejiabang. The Jiangyin gang, along with over forty individuals, including several injured soldiers, attacked him with weapons, causing severe injuries and leaving him covered in blood. Police officers apprehended three injured soldiers: Qiu Hu, Liu Xiu, and Liang Huapei, and sent them to the District Court for detention. Sun further accused Zhang Xiaogen, Huang Guirong, Tao He, Xiaojiangyin, and others from the Jiangyin gang as the main perpetrators, requesting investigation, but the matter remained unresolved. Yesterday morning at 10 a.m., the Jiangyin and Shandong gangs were mediating the dispute inside the Xuejiabang teahouse. Unexpectedly, the Jiangyin gang suddenly gathered two to three hundred people, some with firearms. The Shandong gang was smaller in number, and while they had weapons, they lacked effective tools. A battle broke out, and the Shandong gang was defeated, resulting in three seriously injured and many slightly injured. A man surnamed Li suffered brain damage and is said to have died. The First Precinct of the First District received the report and dispatched a large number of police officers to the scene, detaining over twenty individuals fighting on the spot. Around noon, another Jiangyin man was arrested at Jixiang Lane in front of the District Court. All were detained and sent to the Public Security Bureau, then to the District Court for investigation.

Land Bureau Urges Collection of Land Title Deeds 166

The Municipal Land Bureau has completed the surveying of household land in various districts and prepared the land title deeds to be exchanged by property owners who have transferred ownership. Since the January 28th Incident, many property owners have not collected them. It is now reported that the Bureau has issued a public notice urging collection and has posted a list of property owners' names in front of the Bureau, so that owners who have not yet collected their deeds can check and retrieve them.

Petition from the National Products Exhibition Hall 167

Petition to Be Forwarded to the Mayor – Requesting a General Order to Promote National Products

Cao Zhendong, Director of the Shanghai National Products Exhibition Hall, submitted a document to Director Wu, stating: "Regarding the matter of a petition: National products are the foundation of national production, and promotion is the way to alleviate unemployment. In recent years, all countries have been raising tariffs and revitalizing national products in response to the global economic downturn to mitigate economic panic. For decades, our country has suffered from tariff agreements and economic aggression from imperialists, leading to a state of decline throughout the country. In recent years, the government has established special agencies to guide and promote national products, showing great enthusiasm for this cause. It has also raised its voice and awakened society, hoping to boost sales of national products and save the country from its imminent crisis. However, society still favors extravagance, and the people are superstitious about foreign goods. Despite long-term promotion, the results have been minimal. Currently, various products in our city are gradually reaching maturity. All daily necessities and Chinese and Western clothing have excellent products. Previously, foreign goods were indispensable, but now they are gradually being made domestically. However, due to the public's entrenched habits and lack of understanding of national products, manufacturers still face sales difficulties. In view of this, and noting that since the September 18th Incident, the public's patriotic sentiment has reached a peak, now is the time to promote national products, as the results will certainly be higher than in the past. Moreover, our city is the commercial center of the country, the focus of attention from both China and abroad. Citizens using national products is an example for the whole country in promoting national spirit and alleviating the declining market. The responsibility of our Hall is to learn from past experience, examine the situation, and promote national products. We believe that promotion should have persistence and discernment, with continuous publicity and a spirit of mutual encouragement. Based on these points, we have revised the simplified implementation measures in accordance with the principles of the Ministry's orders and the implementation methods issued by the Municipal Government as follows: (1) All government agencies should, as far as possible, use domestic products for office supplies. Leaders should also encourage civil servants to set an example by using domestic products for both Chinese and Western clothing. For household daily necessities, they should be directed to purchase national products or nationalized products. They should regularly talk to their children and wives about advocating the use of national products to cultivate a psychology and habit of loving national products. (2) The Education Bureau should be responsible for informing all primary and secondary schools before the start of the semester that all school equipment should be domestic products, except for those that are not available or have no substitutes. Student uniforms and underwear should be made purely of domestic products, and school rules should restrict students from purchasing the same foreign goods that are already produced domestically. Cultivate their diligence and love of domestic goods. Before the end of each semester, set a standard for promoting domestic goods in the current season and methods of publicity for students to work on during the holidays. Education inspectors should pay attention to the above points and set them as evaluation standards. Our Hall is collecting and appraising various national products. If you need to use them, you can come to the Hall to inspect them. We will provide convenience at any time to increase promotional efficiency. The above is for your review and approval. We request that it be forwarded to the Municipal Government and ordered to be implemented by all agencies to effectively promote national products. Whether it is appropriate or not, please examine and instruct us to follow."

Minutes of the Aviation Construction Association Council Meeting 168

The Chinese Aviation Construction Association held its second council meeting yesterday at the 9th floor of the Eight Immortals Youth Association. They welcomed Nanjing aviation member Sun Sheng'san and bid farewell to Lin Jiyong, the representative going to Fujian. Council members Zhu Ziqiao, Wu Shan, Li Cishan, Yin Zhiling, Tan Bozhi, Xiong Xiling (represented by Cha Liangjian), Luo Yinpu, Zheng Xitao, Feng Shaoshan (represented by He Yongyuan), Huang Menggui, Wang Chengzhi, He Jiacheng (represented by Yao Shoukang), Zhu Lin (represented by Yin Zhiling), and members Lin Jiyong, Hua Zhenxin, Sun Sheng'san, Chen Boquan, and others, totaling over thirty people, attended. Yin Zhiling was publicly elected as chairman. (1) A welcoming address was given to Sun and Lin. (2) A report was given on the association's affairs, stating that the association aims to promote civil aviation as the foundation for building national defense aviation. Since its establishment, it has received support from all sectors, and the government is also preparing an aviation patriotism association and intends to open up civil aviation. This coincides with the purpose of the initiators of this association. It can be seen that the people of the whole country recognize that developing China's aviation requires opening up civil aviation. Therefore, the association's responsibility is heavy and great. Next, a letter from Brigadier General Weng Zhaoyuan of Zhangzhou was mentioned, reporting on the aviation construction situation in Fujian Province. There are currently seven or eight aircraft, which can be used as the foundation for aviation construction. The report also mentioned the process of the association submitting a document to the Ministry of Military and Political Affairs for registration. (3) Zhu Lin reported on the association's preliminary plan for training aviation personnel and manufacturing talent. (4) Proposals were discussed. (1) A proposal to revise the association's charter was approved. (2) Yin Zhiling and Tan Bozhi were elected as directors of the general affairs group, Zheng Xitao and Yao Shoukang as chairmen of the publicity group, Hu Yunqiu and He Yongyuan as directors of the economic group, and Feng Shaoshan and Jiang Junyi as directors of the membership group. (3) A design committee was organized to plan the association's education, manufacturing, and business sectors. Zhu Lin, Lin Jiyong, Wang Chengzhi, Yin Wenyu, Bu Jiefang, Zhang Zilian, Weng Zhaoyuan, Shen Dexie, Wang Zhitong, Jin Zhixuan, Hu Juewen, Wang Zhiyuan, and Lin Junneng were elected as design committee members. (4) The regulations for soliciting aircraft committee members were approved, and representatives from fifteen groups, including the Chaozhou Native Association Youth Association, were elected as committee members. (5) Lin Jiyong was appointed as representative to Fujian to prepare for the establishment of a branch. (6) Sun Sheng'san was appointed as the membership group's resident executive in Beijing. (7) Lin Wozhang was hired as honorary advisor. Finally, council members Li Cishan, Wu Shan, and Wang Chengzhi, and members Lin Jiyong and Sun Sheng'san, spoke successively, elaborating on the issue of aviation construction in detail. The meeting adjourned at 3 p.m.

Two Public Notices from the Shanghai District Court Regarding Internal Rectification 169

Separate Waiting and Audience

Clarify the Boundaries of the Legal Profession

The Shanghai District Court recently issued two public notices for the purpose of internal rectification: "Public Notice: Litigants coming to the court for questioning should bring their summons and report to the registration office. After reporting, they should wait in separate waiting rooms for questioning. Those who wish to observe the hearing should report the reason for observing and fill in the observer registry form. After obtaining a ticket, they should wait in the observer waiting area and enter the court in order when the case begins. All other irrelevant persons are not allowed to enter without permission, and those who violate this will be investigated. All are to comply. This is hereby notified." "Public Notice: The lawyer's lounge and lawyer's reading room are specifically for lawyers to rest and read documents. The boundaries are very clear. The litigants also have waiting rooms. How can they mix into the lawyer's room or gather in the corridors, causing confusion? In addition to instructing officials to strictly prohibit this at all times, we hereby notify the litigants to comply and not to violate this again. This is hereby notified."

Niu Lan's Defense Attorney, Chen Ying, Went to Beijing Last Night 170

Niu Lan and his wife, after being released from prison for medical treatment on bail by Song Qingling, Cai Yuanpei, and Yang Xingfo, have recovered their health. The Gulou Hospital sent two letters to the court requesting that they be taken back. It was therefore decided to bring them back yesterday to the prison infirmary for medical observation, with the hearing continuing on the 4th. As a result, Niu and his wife resumed their hunger strike. Their defense attorney, Chen Ying, went to Beijing by train last night. Accompanying him was Johnson, a famous lawyer from Geneva hired by the Niu Lan family.

Robbers in West Shanghai Resist Arrest 171

Yu Baoquan, Qin Dianqing, Qin Fugeng, and others, farmers in Yugeng Lane, about three li south of the Hongqiao Town in West Shanghai, were robbed on the night of the 29th of last month. The police bureau is conducting a rigorous investigation. Unexpectedly, Zhang Jinxiang, a Taoist priest residing at No. 20 Zhanggeng Lane, about half a li east of Yujiatang, who was relatively well-off, was also visited by robbers. Around 11 PM the night before last (the 1st), over ten robbers speaking with mixed accents suddenly arrived and surrounded Zhang's front and back doors, shining flashlights through the windows. Zhang Jinxiang had just returned home from a Taoist temple and had not yet gone to sleep. Seeing the light, he knew something was wrong. He heard footsteps and urgent knocking on the door. Knowing it was a robbery, Zhang quickly took a gong and climbed onto the roof from the courtyard using a ladder, ringing the gong and shouting for help. Police Chief Li Guodong of the Hongqiao Town Police Station of the Sixth Precinct, along with patrol officers Wang Yucai and Wang Yilu, were patrolling nearby. Hearing the alarm, they chased after the robbers. The robbers noticed and opened fire to resist arrest. The police chief also drew his gun and returned fire, firing over ten shots. In the end, the robbers, realizing they were outnumbered, fled south. Police Chief Li, due to limited manpower and the darkness of the night, did not dare to pursue them, allowing them to escape. He immediately returned to the station and reported to Police Chief Bi Zhenhua, who yesterday dispatched Inspector Sun to investigate. A spent pistol cartridge was found in the victim's home, and two window panes were broken. Fortunately, the front door was sturdy, and the robbers were unable to enter, so there was no loss. However, the whole family was greatly frightened.

Floating Corpse in the Huangpu River 172

A male corpse floated up yesterday in the Huangpu River west of the Minhang Garden. He was about thirty years old, wearing a white cloth short shirt and old striped cloth trousers. He had floated from Pudong. After examination by the First Branch of the County Public Security Bureau, no injuries were found. Therefore, the matter was referred to the District Court for another examination yesterday.

Taoist Priest Dies of Addiction and Illness 173

Shi Jingding, a Taoist priest from Pudong, around fifty years old, was operating in Shanghai and was addicted to opium. He often went to the Yanzike on the upper floor of the Sishi Chun Noodle Shop at No. 256 Avenue Cardes for his fix. Last month, when the French police raided the premises, Shi was inside and was arrested along with the others. After questioning at the court, the female owner of the opium den was sentenced to imprisonment and fined. Shi, as an opium user, was sentenced to one month of imprisonment and fined 20 yuan. Unable to pay, he was imprisoned for one day for every two yuan owed. He was released at noon on the first of this month, but he was sick due to withdrawal symptoms while in custody. When he was released, he was already in critical condition. He hired a rickshaw to No. 256 Avenue Cardes, but he was unable to move after getting off and sat on the ground. He died shortly after. The police found him and reported it to the police station, which sent a detective to transport the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Hall mortuary. No relatives were found. The Second Special Court was notified yesterday morning and dispatched Wu, an examining coroner, to the mortuary. He confirmed that the deceased died of illness and ordered the body to be handed over to the Tongren Fuyuan Hall for photographing and burial.

The Thief, A Hole in One 174

Jin A'er Fell Upside Down

At around 4 AM yesterday morning, a thief, Jin A'er from Suzhou, somehow managed to climb from the window into the bedroom of Ji Ruibing, a Ningbo native, at No. 3 Huachun Lane, Zhangjia Lane in the city. In the darkness, he stole a cheongsam and silk trousers hanging on the wall and placed them on the windowsill. Because the stolen goods were too few, he was still trying to open the trunk to steal more when Gu, who was asleep in bed, suddenly heard a tapping sound. Knowing something was wrong, he immediately jumped out of bed and turned on the light. In the light, he saw Jin stealing. Jin realized the light had been turned on and that he was in trouble. In his haste, he jumped out the window onto the street. Unexpectedly, as his body left the window, his feet were tripped by the electric wire outside. In an instant, he fell upside down, his head hitting the stone steps, causing a head wound and profuse bleeding. He fell unconscious to the ground. Seeing this, Gu immediately reported it to the Second Precinct of the First District. Police Chief Li went to the scene and found Jin's head had a large hole, and he was in critical condition. He was immediately sent to the hospital for treatment. He also investigated the details of the theft at the Gu residence and reported back to the station.
